               \n                    Rick Mason                \n            \n                                    DeVotchKa frontman Nick Urata croons with a soaring intensity that falls somewhere among Roy Orbison, Bryan Ferry, and some Eastern European circus ringmaster. And his band wears eclecticism like a cloak that has soaked up influences from around the globe, including the cheesy corners of American pop. Among the group's hallmarks is the sometimes fractious juxtaposition of all those elements. That formula leads to startling fusions of, say, Eastern European folk music, mariachi, and cowpoke country with a punk edge. In a move of inspired perversity, the band even teamed up for a time with burlesque icon Dita Von Teese. In the mid-'00s, the group took a more cinematic track, composing the Grammy-nominated soundtrack for Little Miss Sunshine.
